PRACTICE TEST - FE CIVIL 3 - Mathematics and Statistics

1. A simply supported beam has a span length of 10 meters and carries a uniformly distributed load of 5 kN/m. What is the maximum bending moment in the beam?
   A) 125 kNm
   B) 250 kNm
   C) 300 kNm
   D) 500 kNm

2. An engineer discovers a flaw in a completed project. According to engineering ethics, what should the engineer do first?
   A) Notify the relevant authorities immediately.
   B) Consult the client and propose a solution.
   C) Ignore the issue since the project is complete.
   D) Contact a lawyer for legal protection.

3. What is the future worth of $10,000 after 5 years if the annual interest rate is 6% compounded annually?
   A) $11,337
   B) $13,382
   C) $14,050
   D) $15,000

4. A 3-meter-long uniform beam weighs 300 N and is supported at both ends. A 500 N load is placed 1 meter from the left support. What is the reaction force at the right support?
   A) 400 N
   B) 500 N
   C) 600 N
   D) 700 N

5. A car accelerates uniformly from rest to a speed of 20 m/s in 5 seconds. What is the acceleration of the car?
   A) 2 m/s²
   B) 4 m/s²
   C) 5 m/s²
   D) 10 m/s²

6. What is the derivative of f(x) = 3x² + 5x - 7?
   A) 6x + 5
   B) 3x + 5
   C) 6x - 7
   D) 3x²

7. An engineer is asked to approve a design they did not work on or review. What is the ethical action to take?
   A) Approve the design to save time.
   B) Request sufficient time to review the design.
   C) Refuse to approve the design under any circumstances.
   D) Approve the design but note the lack of review.

8. What is the present worth of $1,000 to be received 5 years from now if the interest rate is 8% annually?
   A) $680.58
   B) $735.03
   C) $900.00
   D) $1,080.00

9. A 4-meter-long beam is simply supported at both ends and carries a point load of 500 N at the center. What is the reaction force at one of the supports?
   A) 500 N
   B) 250 N
   C) 1000 N
   D) 0 N

10. A 2 kg object moves in a circular path with a radius of 3 meters at a constant speed of 4 m/s. What is the centripetal force acting on the object?
   A) 8 N
   B) 10.67 N
   C) 12 N
   D) 16 N

11. A steel rod with a cross-sectional area of 0.01 m² is subjected to a tensile force of 50 kN. What is the stress in the rod?
   A) 50 MPa
   B) 5 kPa
   C) 500 kPa
   D) 5 MPa

12. Which material property measures the ability to resist deformation under load?
   A) Ductility
   B) Elastic Modulus
   C) Toughness
   D) Hardness

13. What is the Reynold's number for water flowing at a velocity of 2 m/s in a pipe with a diameter of 0.1 m? Assume kinematic viscosity = 1×10⁻⁶ m²/s.
   A) 20,000
   B) 10,000
   C) 5,000
   D) 2,000

14. How many degrees are in a bearing of N45°E?
   A) 45°
   B) 90°
   C) 135°
   D) 180°

15. What is the primary purpose of a detention basin in stormwater management?
   A) Filter pollutants
   B) Reduce peak discharge rates
   C) Increase groundwater recharge
   D) Provide water for irrigation

16. What is the integral of f(x) = 5x^4 + 3x^2 with respect to x?
   A) x^5 + x^3 + C
   B) x^5 + x^3 + 7
   C) x^5 + 3x^3 + C
   D) (5/5)x^5 + (3/3)x^3 + C

17. An engineer encounters a design flaw that could compromise safety. What is the most ethical course of action?
   A) Ignore the flaw and proceed with the project.
   B) Report the flaw to the relevant stakeholders and suggest corrective measures.
   C) Fix the issue without informing anyone.
   D) Delay the project until someone else notices the flaw.

18. If $5,000 is invested at an annual interest rate of 8% compounded annually, what will be its value after 3 years?
   A) $6,200
   B) $6,349.92
   C) $6,480
   D) $6,509.36

19. A rigid beam is supported by a pin at one end and a roller at the other. A 10 kN load is applied at its midpoint. What is the reaction force at the pin?
   A) 5 kN
   B) 10 kN
   C) 15 kN
   D) 20 kN

20. A 2 kg mass is moving with a velocity of 10 m/s. What is its kinetic energy?
   A) 100 J
   B) 200 J
   C) 300 J
   D) 400 J

21. A cylindrical steel bar with a diameter of 0.02 m is subjected to a tensile load of 10 kN. What is the tensile stress in the bar?
   A) 25 MPa
   B) 31.8 MPa
   C) 35 MPa
   D) 40 MPa

22. Which of the following materials exhibits the most ductile behavior?
   A) Ceramic
   B) Glass
   C) Mild Steel
   D) Concrete

23. Water flows through a pipe with a diameter of 0.3 m at a velocity of 4 m/s. What is the volumetric flow rate?
   A) 0.28 m³/s
   B) 0.36 m³/s
   C) 0.38 m³/s
   D) 0.42 m³/s

24. A line runs due east for 500 meters and then turns 30° north of east for 300 meters. What is the total horizontal displacement?
   A) 750 m
   B) 780 m
   C) 800 m
   D) 810 m

25. What is the primary purpose of a sedimentation basin in water treatment?
   A) To remove dissolved salts
   B) To separate solid particles from water
   C) To kill bacteria
   D) To adjust pH levels

26. What is the solution to the differential equation dy/dx = 3x^2, given that y(0) = 4?
   A) y = x^3 + 4
   B) y = 3x^3 + 4
   C) y = x^3 - 4
   D) y = x^2 + 4

27. An engineer observes an unsafe condition on a construction site. What is their ethical responsibility?
   A) Ignore the situation since it is not their project.
   B) Notify the site supervisor immediately.
   C) Report it to the media.
   D) Wait until an incident occurs to take action.

28. What is the annual worth of an investment that costs $20,000, has a useful life of 5 years, and returns $6,000 annually at an interest rate of 10%?
   A) $4,000
   B) $6,000
   C) $5,000
   D) $3,000

29. A beam is fixed at one end and free at the other. A point load of 500 N is applied at the free end. What is the reaction moment at the fixed end if the beam length is 3 m?
   A) 1500 Nm
   B) 500 Nm
   C) 300 Nm
   D) 1000 Nm

30. A 10 kg object is moving with a velocity of 15 m/s. What is its momentum?
   A) 150 kg·m/s
   B) 1500 kg·m/s
   C) 15 kg·m/s
   D) 100 kg·m/s

31. A steel rod with a cross-sectional area of 0.005 m² is subjected to a tensile force of 100 kN. What is the stress in the rod?
   A) 20 MPa
   B) 200 MPa
   C) 2 MPa
   D) 50 MPa

32. Which of the following is a primary characteristic of ductile materials?
   A) High compressive strength
   B) Large plastic deformation before fracture
   C) Low hardness
   D) Brittle failure

33. Water flows through a 0.2 m diameter pipe at a velocity of 3 m/s. What is the volumetric flow rate?
   A) 0.094 m³/s
   B) 0.19 m³/s
   C) 0.094 m³/s
   D) 0.13 m³/s

34. A line is measured to be 300 m with a 5% slope. What is the horizontal distance?
   A) 285.7 m
   B) 294.1 m
   C) 300 m
   D) 295.5 m

35. What is the primary function of a retention basin in stormwater management?
   A) Filter pollutants
   B) Store water temporarily
   C) Reduce sediment transport
   D) Prevent groundwater infiltration

36. A column is subjected to an axial load of 200 kN and has a cross-sectional area of 0.01 m². What is the axial stress in the column?
   A) 20 MPa
   B) 200 MPa
   C) 2 MPa
   D) 0.2 MPa

37. What is the integral of f(x) = 4x^3 - 2x + 1 with respect to x?
   A) x^4 - x^2 + x + C
   B) x^4 - 2x^2 + x + C
   C) x^4 - 2x^2 + C
   D) 4x^4 - x + C

38. An engineer discovers a major safety issue in a project they are managing. What is their most ethical action?
   A) Ignore the issue to meet the deadline.
   B) Report the issue and halt the project until it is resolved.
   C) Proceed with the project and fix the issue later.
   D) Consult the client and proceed as per their direction.

39. What is the future worth of $15,000 after 3 years at an annual interest rate of 5%, compounded annually?
   A) $16,575
   B) $17,000
   C) $17,362.50
   D) $18,000

40. A 5-meter beam is simply supported at its ends and carries a uniform distributed load of 10 kN/m. What is the reaction at each support?
   A) 10 kN
   B) 25 kN
   C) 50 kN
   D) 100 kN

41. A car accelerates from 10 m/s to 30 m/s in 5 seconds. What is its acceleration?
   A) 2 m/s²
   B) 4 m/s²
   C) 6 m/s²
   D) 8 m/s²

42. A steel bar with a length of 2 meters and cross-sectional area of 0.01 m² is subjected to a tensile force of 100 kN. What is the stress in the bar?
   A) 10 MPa
   B) 50 MPa
   C) 100 MPa
   D) 500 MPa

43. Which material property determines resistance to deformation under stress?
   A) Elasticity

   A) 20,000

45. What is the bearing of a line that runs due east?

   C) 3x^2 - 2x + 7
   D) None of the above

48. An engineer is offered a gift by a supplier during a project. According to the NSPE Code of Ethics, what should they do?
   A) Accept the gift if it has monetary value.
   B) Accept the gift only if it does not influence professional judgment.
   C) Decline the gift regardless of the situation.

78. An engineer discovers a safety issue in a project they are overseeing. What is their ethical responsibility according to the NSPE Code of Ethics?

   A) $13,382.26

   A) Ignore the issue since it is pre-existing.

   D) Wait until the bridge shows signs of immediate danger.

93. What is the present worth (PW) of $10,000 received 5 years from now, at a discount rate of 8% per year?
   A) $6,805.83
   B) $8,000.00
   C) $7,950.00
   D) $9,259.26

94. A 10 m beam is supported at both ends and a 500 N force acts at its midpoint. What is the reaction force at each support?
   A) 500 N at each support
   B) 250 N at each support
   C) 1000 N at each support
   D) 750 N at one support and 250 N at the other

95. A car accelerates uniformly from rest to a velocity of 20 m/s in 10 seconds. What is its acceleration?
   A) 1 m/s²
   B) 2 m/s²
   C) 0.5 m/s²
   D) 10 m/s²

96. A steel rod with a cross-sectional area of 0.002 m² is subjected to a tensile force of 100 kN. What is the stress in the rod?
   A) 50 MPa
   B) 100 MPa
   C) 200 MPa
   D) 500 MPa

97. Which material property measures a material's ability to return to its original shape after deformation?
   A) Ductility
   B) Elasticity
   C) Toughness
   D) Hardness

98. Water flows through a pipe with a velocity of 3 m/s and a diameter of 0.2 m. What is the volumetric flow rate?
   A) 0.094 m³/s
   B) 0.116 m³/s
   C) 0.075 m³/s
   D) 0.126 m³/s

99. A line measures 300 m horizontally, with a slope of 5%. What is the true slope distance?
   A) 300.75 m
   B) 315.00 m
   C) 301.50 m
   D) 309.00 m

100. What is the primary purpose of a grit chamber in a wastewater treatment plant?
   A) To remove dissolved solids
   B) To reduce biological oxygen demand
   C) To remove heavy inorganic particles
   D) To increase aeration

CORRECT ANSWERS AND EXPLANATIONS

1. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: The maximum bending moment for a simply supported beam with a uniform load is given by M = wL^2/8. Substituting w = 5 kN/m and L = 10 m, M = (5 * 10^2) / 8 = 125 kNm.

2. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Engineering ethics requires engineers to prioritize public safety and inform the client of any issues while suggesting solutions.

3. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: Future worth is calculated using F = P(1 + i)^n. Here, P = $10,000, i = 0.06, n = 5. F = 10,000(1 + 0.06)^5 = $14,050.

4. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Using the equation of equilibrium for moments about the left support: (500 * 1) + (300 * 1.5) = R2 * 3, solving gives R2 = 400 N.

5. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Acceleration is given by a = (v - u)/t. Here, u = 0, v = 20 m/s, t = 5 s. a = (20 - 0)/5 = 4 m/s².

6. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: The derivative of 3x² is 6x, the derivative of 5x is 5, and the constant -7 becomes 0.

7. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: According to engineering ethics, designs should only be approved after proper review.

8. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Present Worth = Future Value / (1 + interest rate)^years = 1000 / (1 + 0.08)^5.

9. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: The load is symmetrically distributed, so each support carries half of the load: 500 N / 2 = 250 N.

10. Correct Answer: D
   Explanation: Centripetal Force = (mass × velocity²) / radius = (2 × 4²) / 3 = 16 N.

11. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Stress = Force / Area = 50,000 N / 0.01 m² = 50 × 10⁶ N/m² = 50 MPa.

12. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Elastic modulus quantifies a material's ability to resist elastic deformation under load.

13. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Re = (Velocity × Diameter) / Kinematic Viscosity = (2 × 0.1) / 1×10⁻⁶ = 20,000.

14. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: A bearing of N45°E specifies a 45° angle measured clockwise from the north direction.

15. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Detention basins are designed to temporarily store stormwater to reduce peak discharge rates.

16. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: The integral of 5x^4 is (5/5)x^5 and the integral of 3x^2 is (3/3)x^3. Add the constant of integration, C.

17. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: According to engineering ethics, safety is paramount, and reporting any potential issues is essential for transparency and resolution.

18. Correct Answer: D
   Explanation: Use the compound interest formula: FV = PV(1 + i)^n. Here, FV = 5000(1 + 0.08)^3 = $6,509.36.

19. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: For equilibrium, the pin and roller share the load equally. Each reaction force is 10 kN / 2 = 5 kN.

20. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Kinetic energy is given by KE = 0.5 * m * v^2. Substituting, KE = 0.5 * 2 * (10)^2 = 200 J.

21. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Stress = Force / Area. The area of the bar is πd²/4 = π(0.02)²/4. Stress = 10,000 / Area = 31.8 MPa.

22. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: Mild steel is known for its ductility, allowing it to deform significantly before fracturing.

23. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Volumetric flow rate = Area * Velocity. Area = πd²/4 = π(0.3)²/4. Q = 0.36 m³/s.

24. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: Horizontal displacement = 500 + 300cos(30°). The result is approximately 800 m.

25. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Sedimentation basins allow solid particles to settle out of water due to gravity.

26. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: The integral of 3x^2 is x^3, and adding the constant of integration C, we use the initial condition y(0)=4 to find C=4.

27. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Engineers must prioritize public safety and report unsafe conditions to the responsible party promptly.

28. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: Using the Annual Worth method, subtract the cost per year from the annual return at the given interest rate.

29. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: The reaction moment is calculated as force × distance from the fixed end: 500 N × 3 m = 1500 Nm.

30. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Momentum is calculated as mass × velocity: 10 kg × 15 m/s = 150 kg·m/s.

31. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Stress is force divided by area: 100,000 N / 0.005 m² = 200 MPa.

32. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Ductile materials undergo significant plastic deformation before breaking.

33. Correct Answer: A

PRACTICE TEST - FE CIVIL 3 - ENGINEERING ECONOMICS

1. A company invests $10,000 in a project with an annual interest rate of 5%. What will be the total amount after 3 years if compounded annually?
   A) $11,500
   B) $11,576.25
   C) $12,000
   D) $13,000

2. What is the present worth of $15,000 to be received 5 years from now at a discount rate of 6%?
   A) $10,627.45
   B) $12,000.00
   C) $13,000.00
   D) $14,150.00

3. If a project has annual maintenance costs of $2,000 and an interest rate of 8%, what is the capitalized cost?
   A) $25,000
   B) $20,000
   C) $16,000
   D) $18,000

4. A project requires an initial investment of $50,000 and generates annual revenue of $12,000 for 6 years. What is the rate of return if the salvage value is $5,000?
   A) 12%
   B) 10%
   C) 8%
   D) 6%

5. Using the straight-line depreciation method, what is the annual depreciation for equipment costing $70,000 with a salvage value of $10,000 and a useful life of 10 years?
   A) $6,000
   B) $7,000
   C) $8,000
   D) $5,000

6. A project has an initial cost of $100,000, annual benefits of $30,000, and annual costs of $10,000 over 10 years. What is the benefit-cost ratio?
   A) 3.0
   B) 2.5
   C) 2.0
   D) 1.5

7. A project requires an initial investment of $75,000 and generates $15,000 annual income. What is the payback period?
   A) 4 years
   B) 5 years
   C) 6 years
   D) 8 years

8. What is the future worth of $20,000 invested for 4 years at an annual interest rate of 9% compounded annually?
   A) $28,000
   B) $30,000
   C) $26,048
   D) $29,000

9. Which of the following factors is NOT considered when determining the economic life of equipment?
   A) Maintenance costs
   B) Salvage value
   C) Depreciation
   D) Market conditions

10. A machine costs $80,000 to purchase and has annual operating costs of $10,000. A new machine costs $120,000 but reduces annual operating costs to $5,000. Which criterion determines the replacement decision?
   A) Initial cost
   B) Operating costs
   C) Cash flow difference
   D) Salvage value

11. A company plans to invest $25,000 in a piece of equipment that will save $6,000 annually in operating costs. If the equipment has a lifespan of 10 years and the company uses an interest rate of 7%, what is the net present value (NPV) of this investment?
   A) $10,000
   B) $15,530
   C) $18,420
   D) $20,000

12. A project has an initial investment of $40,000 and is expected to generate $8,000 annually for 8 years. If the company uses an annual discount rate of 5%, what is the payback period?
   A) 5 years
   B) 6 years
   C) 7 years
   D) 8 years

13. What is the equivalent annual cost (EAC) of a machine that costs $20,000 upfront, has an annual operating cost of $3,000, and a lifespan of 5 years? Assume a discount rate of 6%.
   A) $6,200
   B) $7,000
   C) $5,800
   D) $4,000

14. A company is evaluating two alternatives: Machine A costs $50,000 with annual costs of $10,000, while Machine B costs $60,000 with annual costs of $8,000. Both have a lifespan of 8 years. Considering a discount rate of 5%, which machine is more economically viable?
   A) Machine A
   B) Machine B
   C) Both are equally viable
   D) Neither is viable

   A) $82,000
   B) $85,000
   C) $88,000
   D) $90,000

   A) 5.5%
   B) 6.2%
   C) 7.0%
   D) 8.1%

   B) Option 2
   C) Both are equivalent
   D) Cannot be determined

100. What is the Equivalent Annual Cost (EAC) of a machine with a first cost of $90,000, annual operating costs of $15,000, and a salvage value of $10,000 over a 5-year life at a discount rate of 4%?
   A) $25,000
   B) $26,480
   C) $27,920
   D) $28,900



--- CORRECT ANSWERS AND EXPLANATIONS ---

1. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: The formula for compound interest is A = P(1 + r)^t. Substituting the values: A = $10,000(1 + 0.05)^3 = $11,576.25.

2. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: The formula for present worth is PW = F / (1 + i)^t. Substituting the values: PW = $15,000 / (1 + 0.06)^5 = $10,627.45.

3. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Capitalized cost is calculated as CC = A / i. Substituting: CC = $2,000 / 0.08 = $20,000.

4. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: The rate of return is calculated using trial and error with the IRR formula: NPV = 0. Here, 8% provides the closest balance.

5. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Straight-line depreciation is calculated as (Cost - Salvage) / Useful life. ($70,000 - $10,000) / 10 = $6,000.

6. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: Benefit-cost ratio = (Total benefits / Total costs). Here, BCR = ($30,000*10) / ($100,000 + $10,000*10) = 2.0.

7. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: Payback period = Initial investment / Annual income. $75,000 / $15,000 = 5 years.

8. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: Future worth is calculated as FW = P(1 + i)^t. Substituting: FW = $20,000(1 + 0.09)^4 = $26,048.

9. Correct Answer: D
   Explanation: Economic life considers costs directly tied to the asset, not external factors like market conditions.

10. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: Replacement decisions focus on the cash flow difference and cost savings over time.

11. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: The NPV is calculated by subtracting the initial investment from the present worth of the annual savings using the interest rate and lifespan. The formula for present worth of an annuity is used.

12. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: The payback period is calculated by dividing the initial investment by the annual revenue. In this case: $40,000 / $8,000 = 5 years.

13. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: EAC is calculated by dividing the present worth of the machine cost and operating costs over its lifespan using the given discount rate.

14. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: To compare the alternatives, the total present worth of costs over the lifespan of each machine is calculated using the discount rate. Machine B has a lower total cost.

15. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: The present value formula is used to determine the amount to invest today: PV = FV / (1 + i)^n.

16. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: The compound interest formula FV = PV * (1 + i)^n is used to solve for the annual interest rate.

17. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: The present value of Option 2 is calculated and compared to Option 1 to determine which has higher present worth.

18. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: The salvage value is calculated by subtracting the total depreciation from the initial cost of the machine.

19. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: The correct formula for the capital recovery factor is derived from the annuity formula and accounts for the interest rate and duration.

20. Correct Answer: D
   Explanation: The future worth is calculated using the future value of an annuity formula: FW = P * [(1+i)^n - 1] / i.

21. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: The net present value (NPV) is calculated using the formula: NPV = Σ(CF/(1+r)^t) - initial investment, where CF is the cash flow, r is the interest rate, and t is the time period. Discount each cash flow to present value and sum them, then subtract the initial investment.

22. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: The EAC is calculated by finding the present value of costs and dividing by the annuity factor. Include the initial cost, annual costs, and salvage value discounted over the life span.

23. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: The IRR is the discount rate that equates the present value of cash inflows to the initial investment. Use iterative calculation methods or financial calculators to solve for IRR.

24. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Profitability Index (PI) is calculated as the ratio of the present value of cash inflows to the initial investment. Discount the cash flows using the given interest rate and compute the PI.

25. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Straight-line depreciation calculates yearly depreciation as (Initial Cost - Salvage Value) / Useful Life. Multiply the yearly depreciation by the number of years to find the accumulated depreciation, then subtract from the initial cost.

26. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Use the sinking fund factor (SFF) formula to determine the annual deposit: SFF = i / [(1+i)^n - 1], where i is the interest rate and n is the number of years. Multiply the SFF by the desired future value.

27. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: Calculate the breakeven period by comparing the present worth of costs for each alternative over time to determine when the total costs of the new machine equal the current machine.

28. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: The payback period is calculated by dividing the cumulative cash inflows by the initial investment, considering discounted cash flows if applicable.

29. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: The present worth (PW) is calculated by discounting each payment back to the present using the formula PW = Σ(FV/(1+r)^t), where FV represents each future value, r is the interest rate, and t is the time period.

30. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Discounted payback period accounts for the time it takes for cumulative discounted cash flows to recover the initial investment. Use the formula for discounted cash flows and sum until the initial cost is covered.

31. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: The formula for future worth is F = P(1 + i)^n, where P = $20,000, i = 0.06, and n = 8. F = 20000(1.06)^8 = $32,000.

32. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Use the formula for present worth: P = F / (1 + i)^n, where F = $30,000, i = 0.05, and n = 10. P = 30000 / (1.05)^10 ≈ $18,432.

33. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: NPV is calculated as the present worth of cash flows minus the initial investment. For Option A: NPV = (7000 * P/A, 6%, 10) - 50000 ≈ $7,000 * 7.360 - $50,000 = $51,520 - $50,000 = $1,520. For Option B: NPV = (10000 * P/A, 6%, 10) - 70000 ≈ $10,000 * 7.360 - $70,000 = $73,600 - $70,000 = $3,600.

34. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Double declining balance method uses 2/Life * Current Book Value = 2/10 * $100,000 = $20,000.

35. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Payback period is calculated as (Cost of New Machine - Salvage Value of Old Machine) / Annual Savings. ($120,000 - $10,000) / ($15,000 - $8,000) = $110,000 / $7,000 ≈ 10 years.

36. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: EAC = (Initial Cost * A/P + Annual Maintenance Cost). A/P factor for 7% and 8 years ≈ 0.174. EAC = ($50,000 * 0.174) + $5,000 = $8,700 + $5,000 = $10,175.

37. Correct Answer: D
   Explanation: CRF = i(1+i)^n / [(1+i)^n - 1]. CRF for 5% and 6 years is approximately 0.1938. Annual Payment = $100,000 * 0.1938 = $19,380.

39. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: NPV = (Annual Cash Inflows * P/A factor) - Initial Investment. P/A factor for 8% over 5 years ≈ 3.993. NPV = (40,000 * 3.993) - 150,000 = $159,720 - $150,000 = $22,500.

   Explanation: IRR is the discount rate at which NPV equals zero. Using trial and error or financial software, IRR is found to be approximately 14%.

42. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: SYD = n(n+1)/2 = 5(5+1)/2 = 15. Year 3 depreciation: (Remaining years / SYD) * Depreciable amount = (3/15) * ($100,000 - $10,000) = $18,000.

   Explanation: The size of each installment is calculated using the formula for an annuity: A = P × (i(1+i)^n) / ((1+i)^n − 1). Substituting P = $1,000,000, i = 0.05, and n = 15, the annual installment is approximately $91,565.

88. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: The Present Worth (PW) is calculated using the formula PW = A × (P/A, i%, n). Using a discount rate of 10% and a time span of 6 years, the PW is approximately $75,000.

89. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: EAC is calculated as the annualized cost of the initial investment over its useful life. Using (A/P, 6%, 8 years), the EAC is approximately $73,809.

90. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Double declining depreciation is calculated as 2 × Straight-line rate × Book value. For year 2, the book value is reduced by the first year's depreciation, resulting in a second-year depreciation expense of $40,000.

91. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: To calculate NPV, sum the discounted cash flows over the project's lifespan and subtract the initial investment. NPV formula: NPV = Σ (Cash Flow / (1 + Discount Rate)^n) - Initial Investment.

92. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Straight-line depreciation formula: (Initial Cost - Salvage Value) / Useful Life. In this case, ($180,000 - $20,000) / 10 = $15,000.

93. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: Use the formula for annuity payments: P = [r * PV] / [1 - (1 + r)^(-n)], where r is the interest rate, PV is the loan amount, and n is the number of periods.

94. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Calculate NPV for both options using the formula: NPV = Σ (Cash Flow / (1 + Discount Rate)^n) - Initial Investment. Option A has a higher NPV due to larger annual savings despite a shorter duration.

95. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Future value of an ordinary annuity formula: FV = P * [(1 + r)^n - 1] / r. Substitute P = $20,000, r = 0.06, n = 15.

96. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Present Worth formula: PW = Σ [(Net Cash Flow) / (1 + Discount Rate)^n] - Initial Cost. Net Cash Flow = Revenue - Maintenance Cost.

97. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: Capital Recovery cost = Annual Expenses + (Discount Rate * Initial Cost). Substitute Annual Expenses = $25,000, Discount Rate = 0.06, Initial Cost = $300,000.

98. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: The IRR is the discount rate that makes the Net Present Value (NPV) of cash flows equal to zero. Iterative methods or financial calculators are typically used.

99. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: Profit = (Selling Price - Variable Cost) * Units - Fixed Costs. Substitute values: ($25 - $10) * 25,000 - $150,000.

100. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: EAC is calculated using: EAC = [PW of costs] / [Annuity factor for n, r]. First calculate PV, then divide by annuity factor.

PRACTICE TEST - FE CIVIL 3 - STATICS

1. A 10 kN force is applied at a 30° angle to the horizontal. What is the horizontal component of the force?
   A) 5 kN
   B) 8.66 kN
   C) 10 kN
   D) 15 kN

   D) 500 N down

   D) 200 N downward

97. A uniform rod of length 5 m and weight 50 N is pinned at one end and held horizontally with a 120 N force applied at the other end. What is the reaction force at the pinned end?
   A) 50 N
   B) 120 N
   C) 170 N
   D) 85 N

98. A steel truss structure has 14 members and 9 joints. Is this truss statically determinate?
   A) Yes
   B) No, it is statically indeterminate
   C) No, it is unstable
   D) Cannot be determined

99. A beam of 10 m length is fixed at both ends and subjected to a uniformly distributed load of 4 kN/m. What is the total load on the beam?
   A) 20 kN
   B) 30 kN
   C) 40 kN
   D) 50 kN

100. A cable is suspended between two supports at the same elevation, carrying a point load at its center. What is the tension in the cable at the midpoint?
   A) Equal to the load
   B) Less than the load
   C) Greater than the load
   D) Zero



--- CORRECT ANSWERS AND EXPLANATIONS ---

1. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: The horizontal component of the force is calculated as F*cos(θ). Here, F = 10 kN and θ = 30°. Horizontal component = 10*cos(30°) = 10*0.866 = 8.66 kN.

2. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: For static equilibrium, the sum of forces must equal zero. The upward force (200 N) and downward force (300 N) result in a net downward force of 100 N. To maintain equilibrium, a 100 N upward force is required.

3. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: Moment = Force * Distance. Here, Moment = 50 N * 2 m = 100 Nm.

4. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: The centroid of a uniform rectangular plate is located at the geometric center because the material is distributed uniformly.

5. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: In a 2D truss structure, three equilibrium equations (ΣFx = 0, ΣFy = 0, ΣM = 0) can be used to solve for unknown forces.

6. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: Total load = Load intensity * Length = 5 kN/m * 10 m = 50 kN.

7. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: For a 2D frame, the condition for static determinacy is m + r = 2j (where m = members, r = reactions, j = joints). Here, m = 5, r = 3 (assumed simple supports), and j = 4. Thus, 5 + 3 = 2*4, so the frame is statically determinate.

8. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: The resultant force of a triangular distributed load = 0.5 * base * height. Here, the base = 6 m and height = 4 kN/m. Resultant force = 0.5 * 6 * 4 = 12 kN.

9. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Maximum static friction = μs * Normal force. The normal force = Weight of the block = m*g = 100*9.8 = 980 N. Maximum static friction = 0.4*980 = 392 N.

10. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: For a point load at mid-span on a simply supported beam, the reactions at both supports are equal and can be calculated as R = P/2 = 20/2 = 10 kN.

11. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Using the equilibrium equations, sum of moments about the pin gives the reaction force at the roller as 10 kN.

12. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: The centroid of a triangle is located at 1/3 the height from the base and at the center of the base width.

13. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: The truss satisfies the equation 2J = M + R (where J = number of joints, M = number of members, R = reaction forces), indicating it is statically determinate.

14. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: The moment at the fixed support is calculated as force × distance, i.e., 10 kN × 4 m = 40 kNm.

15. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: The frictional force is greater than the component of gravitational force parallel to the incline, hence the block remains stationary.

16. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: The total load is calculated as (1/2 × base × height) = (1/2 × 8 m × 6 kN/m) = 24 kN.

17. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: The total load is 4 kN/m × 10 m = 40 kN, equally distributed between the two supports as 20 kN each.

18. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: The vertical component is calculated using F × sin(θ). Here, 50 × sin(45°) = 25 N.

19. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: The frame satisfies the equation 2J = M + R, indicating it is statically determinate.

20. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: The force is calculated as Torque / Radius, i.e., 100 Nm / 2 m = 50 N.

21. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: By summing moments about the roller support, the reaction force at the pinned support is calculated as 22.5 kN.

22. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: The location of the resultant force for a triangular load is at two-thirds of the base from the smaller intensity side.

23. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: The reaction force at the left support is calculated using the equilibrium equation for moments about the right support.

24. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: The moment at the fixed support is calculated as the total load multiplied by half the length of the beam (center of gravity of the load).

25. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: The downhill force due to gravity exceeds the maximum static friction force, causing the block to slide.

26. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: The truss is statically determinate as it satisfies the equation m + r = 2j, where m is the number of members, r is the number of reactions, and j is the number of joints.

27. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: The maximum static friction force is calculated as μ × normal force = 0.6 × (50 × 9.81) = 300 N.

28. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: The total load on the beam is calculated as the load intensity multiplied by the span length, which is equally shared by both supports.

29. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: The centroid of a rectangle with uniform mass distribution is located at the geometric center: (L/2, W/2).

30. Correct Answer: D
   Explanation: In equilibrium, all forces and moments must sum to zero.

31. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Torque is calculated by multiplying the force by the perpendicular distance to the axis of rotation: T = F × d.

32. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Using the equilibrium of forces and moments, the horizontal reaction is determined by resolving the weight and geometry of the ladder.

33. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: The vertical reaction at the right support is calculated using the equilibrium equations for forces and moments.

34. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: A statically determinate frame satisfies m + r = 2j, meaning it has 3 degrees of freedom.

46. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Calculate the downslope force as F_down = W × sin(θ) = 200 × sin(20°) ≈ 68.4 N. The friction force is F_friction = μ × W × cos(θ) = 0.3 × 200 × cos(20°) ≈ 56.4 N. Since F_down > F_friction, the block will slide.

PRACTICE TEST - FE CIVIL 3 - DYNAMICS

1. A particle moves along a straight line with a velocity given by v(t) = 3t² - 6t + 2. What is the acceleration of the particle at t = 2 seconds?
   A) 6 m/s²
   B) 10 m/s²
   C) 12 m/s²
   D) 14 m/s²

2. A car of mass 1500 kg accelerates uniformly from rest to a velocity of 20 m/s in 10 seconds. What is the average force acting on the car?
   A) 3000 N
   B) 4000 N
   C) 6000 N
   D) 7500 N

3. A block of mass 5 kg is pushed across a surface with a constant force of 20 N over a distance of 10 m. The coefficient of kinetic friction between the block and the surface is 0.2. What is the net work done on the block?
   A) 200 J
   B) 130 J
   C) 70 J
   D) 0 J

4. A ball of mass 0.5 kg moving at 10 m/s strikes a wall and rebounds with a velocity of -6 m/s. What is the impulse exerted by the wall on the ball?
   A) 3 N·s
   B) 5 N·s
   C) 8 N·s
   D) 12 N·s

5. A wheel of radius 0.5 m rotates with an angular velocity of 4 rad/s. What is the linear velocity of a point on the circumference of the wheel?
   A) 1 m/s
   B) 2 m/s
   C) 4 m/s
   D) 8 m/s

6. A disk of mass 2 kg and radius 1 m is acted upon by a torque of 4 N·m. What is the angular acceleration of the disk?
   A) 2 rad/s²
   B) 4 rad/s²
   C) 8 rad/s²
   D) 16 rad/s²

7. A spring with a stiffness constant of 100 N/m is compressed by 0.2 m. What is the potential energy stored in the spring?
   A) 2 J
   B) 4 J
   C) 5 J
   D) 10 J

8. An object of mass 5 kg moving at 8 m/s collides elastically with another object of mass 3 kg at rest. What is the velocity of the 5 kg object after collision?
   A) 3 m/s
   B) 4 m/s
   C) 5.2 m/s
   D) 6 m/s

9. A ladder weighing 150 N is leaning against a wall at an angle of 60°. What is the horizontal reaction force at the base of the ladder?
   A) 75 N
   B) 130 N
   C) 150 N
   D) 173 N

10. A pendulum of mass 2 kg is raised to a height of 0.8 m. What is its potential energy relative to the lowest point?
   A) 8 J
   B) 16 J
   C) 20 J
   D) 25 J

11. A car accelerates uniformly along a straight road. Its initial velocity is 5 m/s, and it reaches a velocity of 25 m/s in 10 seconds. What is the total distance traveled during this time?
   A) 100 m
   B) 150 m
   C) 200 m
   D) 250 m

12. A 10 kg block is pushed up an inclined plane with an angle of 30° to the horizontal. If the applied force is 100 N parallel to the incline and friction is negligible, what is the acceleration of the block?
   A) 5.0 m/s²
   B) 6.6 m/s²
   C) 7.3 m/s²
   D) 8.7 m/s²

13. A 15 kg cart is pushed with a constant force of 50 N over a distance of 20 m along a frictionless surface. What is the work done on the cart?
   A) 750 J
   B) 1000 J
   C) 1200 J
   D) 1500 J

14. A uniform rod of length 2 m and mass 8 kg is pivoted at one end and set into rotational motion. What is its moment of inertia about the pivot?
   A) 10.7 kg·m²
   B) 12.4 kg·m²
   C) 16.0 kg·m²
   D) 21.3 kg·m²

15. A 5 kg mass is attached to a spring with a stiffness constant of 200 N/m. What is the natural frequency of the spring-mass system?
   A) 0.63 Hz
   B) 1.59 Hz
   C) 3.18 Hz
   D) 5.02 Hz

16. A 2 kg ball traveling at 8 m/s strikes a stationary 3 kg ball in an elastic collision. What is the velocity of the 2 kg ball after the collision?
   A) 2 m/s
   B) -4 m/s
   C) 5 m/s
   D) 6 m/s

17. A car of mass 1200 kg travels around a circular track of radius 50 m at a speed of 10 m/s. What is the magnitude of the centripetal force acting on the car?
   A) 1200 N
   B) 1800 N
   C) 2400 N
   D) 3000 N

18. A solid sphere of mass 2 kg and radius 0.5 m rotates at an angular velocity of 10 rad/s. What is its angular momentum?
   A) 1 kg·m²/s
   B) 2 kg·m²/s
   C) 2.5 kg·m²/s
   D) 5 kg·m²/s

19. A projectile is launched from the ground at an angle of 45° with an initial velocity of 20 m/s. What is the maximum height it reaches?
   A) 5.1 m
   B) 10.2 m
   C) 15.3 m
   D) 20.4 m

20. A 4 kg object moving at 6 m/s collides perfectly inelastically with a 2 kg object moving at 2 m/s in the same direction. What is their combined velocity after the collision?
   A) 3.33 m/s
   B) 4.00 m/s
   C) 4.67 m/s
   D) 5.00 m/s

21. A car initially at rest accelerates uniformly at 3 m/s² for 5 seconds. What is the distance it travels during this time?
   A) 25 m
   B) 37.5 m
   C) 50 m
   D) 75 m

22. A 10 kg block is being pulled on a horizontal surface with a force of 50 N at an angle of 30° above the horizontal. The coefficient of kinetic friction between the block and the surface is 0.2. What is the acceleration of the block?
   A) 0.8 m/s²
   B) 1.2 m/s²
   C) 2.0 m/s²
   D) 3.0 m/s²

   A) 1.0 m/s

100. A projectile is launched at an angle of 30° with an initial velocity of 25 m/s. How long does it remain in the air?
   A) 2.55 s
   B) 3.75 s
   C) 4.25 s
   D) 5.10 s



--- CORRECT ANSWERS AND EXPLANATIONS ---

1. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Acceleration is the derivative of velocity, a(t) = dv/dt = 6t - 6. At t = 2, a(2) = 6(2) - 6 = 6 m/s².

2. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: Force is given by F = ma. First, calculate acceleration: a = (v - u)/t = (20 - 0)/10 = 2 m/s². Then, F = 1500 × 2 = 3000 N.

3. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Work done = Force × Distance. Friction force = μ × m × g = 0.2 × 5 × 9.8 = 9.8 N. Net force = 20 - 9.8 = 10.2 N. Net work = 10.2 × 10 = 130 J.

4. Correct Answer: D
   Explanation: Impulse = Change in momentum = m(v_final - v_initial) = 0.5(-6 - 10) = -8 N·s. Impulse magnitude is 12 N·s.

5. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: Linear velocity v = rω = 0.5 × 4 = 2 m/s.

6. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Torque τ = Iα. For a disk, I = (1/2)mr² = (1/2)(2)(1)² = 1 kg·m². α = τ/I = 4/1 = 4 rad/s².

7. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Potential energy U = (1/2)kx² = (1/2)(100)(0.2)² = 2 J.

8. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Using elastic collision equations and conservation laws, solve for the final velocity of the 5 kg object. Simplified calculation gives v = 4 m/s.

9. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Horizontal reaction force is determined by resolving forces using trigonometric components and equilibrium conditions. Force = 150 × cos(60°) = 75 N.

10. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Potential energy U = mgh = 2 × 9.8 × 0.8 = 15.68 J. Rounded to 16 J.

11. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: The total distance can be calculated using the equation: s = (v₀ + v) * t / 2. Plugging in values: s = (5 + 25) * 10 / 2 = 200 m.

12. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Net force = Applied force - weight component along the incline. F_net = 100 - (10)(9.81)(sin 30°). Acceleration = F_net / mass = 6.6 m/s².

13. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Work = Force × Distance. W = 50 × 20 = 1000 J.

14. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: For a uniform rod pivoted at one end, the moment of inertia is I = (1/3)ML². I = (1/3)(8)(2²) = 10.7 kg·m².

15. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Natural frequency is given by f = (1/2π)√(k/m). f = (1/2π)√(200/5) ≈ 1.59 Hz.

16. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Using conservation of momentum and energy for elastic collisions, the velocity of the 2 kg ball is determined to be -4 m/s.

17. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: Centripetal force is given by F = mv²/r. F = (1200)(10²)/50 = 2400 N.

18. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: The moment of inertia of a solid sphere is I = (2/5)MR². L = Iω = (2/5)(2)(0.5²)(10) = 2.5 kg·m²/s.

19. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Maximum height is given by H = (v₀²sin²θ)/(2g). H = (20²sin²45°)/(2*9.8) ≈ 10.2 m.

20. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Using conservation of momentum: (4 * 6) + (2 * 2) = (4 + 2)v. v = 3.33 m/s.

21. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: The distance traveled under uniform acceleration is given by s = (1/2) * a * t². Substituting a = 3 m/s² and t = 5 s, we get s = (1/2) * 3 * 5² = 37.5 m.

22. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: The net force is calculated by subtracting frictional force from the horizontal component of the applied force. F_net = 50cos(30°) - (0.2)(10)(9.8). Acceleration a = F_net/m = 1.2 m/s².

23. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Using energy conservation, mgh = (1/2)mv². Substituting h = 4 m, g = 9.8 m/s², we solve for v and get v = sqrt(2 * 9.8 * 4) = 6.3 m/s.

24. Correct Answer: D
   Explanation: Using conservation of momentum: (2)(5) + (4)(-2) = (2+4)v. Solving for v gives v = -0.5 m/s.

25. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Using conservation of energy with rotational kinetic energy: mgh = (1/2)mv² + (1/2)Iω². Substituting I = (1/2)mr² and solving gives v = 5.4 m/s.

26. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: The angular frequency is ω = 2πf. Using ω = sqrt(k/m), substituting f = 2 Hz and k = 50 N/m, solving for m gives m = 1.59 kg.

27. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: The time to hit the ground is t = sqrt(2h/g). Substituting h = 50 m, g = 9.8 m/s², t = 3.19 s. The horizontal distance is x = vt = (10)(3.19) = 31.6 m.

28. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Using centripetal force: T + mg = mv²/r at the top. Substituting m = 0.5 kg, v = 4 m/s, r = 1.2 m, g = 9.8 m/s², we get T = 6.7 N.

29. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: Using energy conservation: mgh = (1/2)kx². Substituting m = 1 kg, g = 9.8 m/s², h = 5 m, k = 400 N/m, solving for x gives x = 0.31 m.

30. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Angular momentum L = Iω. For a disk, I = (1/2)mr². Substituting m = 5 kg, r = 0.4 m, ω = 10 rad/s, we get L = 4.0 kg·m²/s.

31. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: Impulse = Δp = FΔt. Change in momentum Δp = m(vf - vi) = 0.1(-20 - 30). Solving for F gives F = 500 N.

32. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: The distance covered can be calculated using the equation: s = 0.5 * a * t². With a = 2 m/s² and t = 20 s, s = 0.5 * 2 * (20²) = 400 m.

33. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: First, calculate the net force in the horizontal direction: F_x = 30 - 10 = 20 N. In the vertical direction, F_y = 20 N. The resultant force is sqrt(20² + 20²) = 28.28 N. The acceleration is a = F/m = 28.28 / 10 = 2.83 m/s².

34. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: The work done against gravity is W = m * g * h. Here, m = 15 kg, g = 9.81 m/s², and h = 5 m. So, W = 15 * 9.81 * 5 = 735 J.

35. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: For elastic collisions, momentum and kinetic energy are conserved. Using these principles, the velocities after collision can be calculated. The 3 kg object's velocity is found to be 2 m/s.

36. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: The rotational kinetic energy is given by KE = 0.5 * I * ω², where I = 0.5 * m * r² and ω = 2π * n/60. Substituting m = 50 kg, r = 0.2 m, and n = 600 rpm, KE = 628 J.

37. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: The centripetal force is F = m * v² / r. Substituting m = 2 kg, v = 4 m/s, and r = 3 m, F = 2 * (4²) / 3 = 16 N.

38. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: The period of oscillation is T = 2π * sqrt(m/k). Substituting m = 2 kg and k = 1000 N/m, T = 0.28 s.

39. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Using conservation of energy, the potential energy at the top is converted to kinetic energy at the bottom. mgh = 0.5 * m * v². Solving for v: v = sqrt(2 * g * h) = sqrt(2 * 9.81 * 2) = 4 m/s.

40. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Impulse = Change in momentum = F * Δt. Rearranging: F = (m * Δv) / Δt. Δv = 5 m/s (initial) - 0 m/s (final), m = 0.2 kg, Δt = 0.01 s. F = (0.2 * 5) / 0.01 = 200 N.

41. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: The work done is W = m * g * h = 100 * 9.81 * 8 = 7848 J. Power is P = W/t. Rearranging for t: t = W/P = 7848 / 500 = 12.5 s.

42. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: To find the time when velocity is maximum, take the derivative of v(t) and set it to zero: dv/dt = 6 - 6t = 0. Solving for t gives t = 1 second.

43. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Since the box moves at a constant speed, Tension = Weight component along the incline = m * g * sin(30°) = 50 * 9.81 * 0.5 = 300 N.

44. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: The potential energy lost by the object equals the spring's elastic potential energy: mgh = 0.5 * k * x². Solving for k: k = (2 * 9.81 * 10) / (0.5²) = 784 N/m.

45. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: Using conservation of momentum: (3 * 5) + (2 * 0) = (3 + 2) * v, v = 15 / 5 = 2.5 m/s.

46. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Using the equation for rolling objects: a = (g * sinθ) / (1 + I/(m*r²)), where I = 0.5 * m * r² for a solid cylinder. For θ = 30°, a = (9.81 * 0.5) / (1 + 0.5) = 3.27 m/s².

47. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Centripetal acceleration is given by a_c = ω²r. Substituting ω = 3 rad/s and r = 2 m, a_c = 3² * 2 = 18 m/s².

48. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: Power = Work / Time = (m * g * h) / t = (500 * 9.81 * 20) / 10 = 9800 W.

49. Correct Answer: D
   Explanation: For elastic collisions, use conservation of momentum and energy. Solving gives the 0.2 kg object a velocity of -9 m/s.

50. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: For a solid cylinder, I = 0.5 * m * r² = 0.5 * 20 * 0.5² = 5 kg·m².

51. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Horizontal acceleration: a_x = (F * cosθ) / m = (40 * cos(60°)) / 5 = 20 / 5 = 4 m/s².

52. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Use the equation v = u + at. Here, initial velocity u = 0, acceleration a = 2 m/s², and time t = 6 seconds. Thus, v = 0 + (2)(6) = 12 m/s.

53. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Frictional force = µ * Normal force = 0.3 * 100 = 30 N. Net force = Applied force - Frictional force = 50 - 30 = 20 N. Acceleration = F/m = 20/10 = 2 m/s².

54. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Use the energy conservation equation or kinematic equation v² = u² + 2gh. Here, u = 0, g = 9.8 m/s², and h = 10 m. v² = 0 + 2(9.8)(10) = 196. v = √196 = 14 m/s.

55. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Impulse = Change in momentum. Initial momentum = 5 * 10 = 50 Ns. Final momentum = 5 * -6 = -30 Ns. Impulse = |-30 - 50| = 80 Ns.

56. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: Work done = F * d * cos θ = 60 * 5 * cos(30°). cos(30°) ≈ 0.866, so work = 60 * 5 * 0.866 ≈ 260 J.

57. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Centripetal force = (m*v²)/r. Here, m = 0.5 kg, v = 4 m/s, r = 2 m. Force = (0.5 * 16)/2 = 8 N.

58. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Relative velocity = Velocity of A - Velocity of B = 30 - 20 = 10 m/s.

59. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Potential energy in a spring = (1/2) * k * x². Here, k = 100 N/m, x = 0.5 m. Energy = (1/2) * 100 * (0.5)² = 25 J.

60. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Maximum height = (v₀² * sin²θ) / (2*g). Here v₀ = 20 m/s, θ = 45°, g = 9.8 m/s². Height = (20² * sin²(45)) / (2 * 9.8). sin(45) ≈ 0.707, so height ≈ 10 m.

61. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Net force = m_A * g - tension. Using equations of motion and Newton's second law, solve for acceleration a ≈ 2 m/s².

62. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Torque = Force * Radius. Rearranging, Force = Torque / Radius. F = 30 / 0.5 = 60 N.

63. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Work done = F * d * cos θ. θ = angle of incline. Use frictional force for net work done calculation. Approximate to solve.

64. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Angular momentum = I * ω. Moment of inertia of disk = (1/2) * m * r². I = 0.5 * 2 * (0.25)² = 0.0625 kg·m². Angular momentum = 0.0625 * 10 = 2.5 kg·m²/s.

65. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: In elastic collisions, use the conservation of momentum and kinetic energy equations to solve for the final velocities. Substitute values to find the result.

66. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: Using the equation v = u + at, where final velocity v = 0, initial velocity u = 8 m/s, and acceleration a = -2 m/s². Solving for time t: 0 = 8 - 2t ⟹ t = 4 seconds.

67. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Work done is given by W = mgh. Here, m = 50 kg, g = 9.8 m/s², and h = 10 m. W = 50 × 9.8 × 10 = 4900 J.

68. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Using conservation of momentum: 4(5) + 3(0) = 4(3) + 3v₂ ⟹ v₂ = 3.67 m/s.

69. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Using the rotational kinematic equation ω = ω₀ + αt, where ω = 0, ω₀ = 20 rad/s, and α = -5 rad/s². Solving for t: 0 = 20 - 5t ⟹ t = 4 seconds.

70. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Time to fall is √(2h/g): t = √(2 × 20 / 9.8) ≈ 2.02 s. Horizontal distance x = vt = 15 × 2.02 ≈ 42.2 m.

71. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Centripetal force F = mv²/r = (1000 × 20²) / 50 = 8000 N.

72. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Period T = 2π√(L/g), where L = 2 m, g = 9.8 m/s². T = 2π√(2/9.8) ≈ 2.83 s.

73. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Using Newton's second law: F = ma ⟹ a = F/m = 36/12 = 3 m/s².

74. Correct Answer: D
   Explanation: Power P = Work/time ⟹ P = 1000/5 = 200 W.

75. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: Maximum static friction force F = μN, where N = mg = 20 × 9.8 = 196 N. F = 0.4 × 196 = 78.4 N.

76. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Acceleration is the derivative of velocity. v(t) = 5t - t², so a(t) = dv/dt = 5 - 2t. At t = 3, a(3) = 5 - 2(3) = 1 m/s².

77. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Use Newton's second law: F = ma. a = F/m = 10/2 = 5 m/s². Using v = u + at, where u = 0, v = 0 + (5)(5) = 25 m/s.

78. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Using conservation of energy, PE_top = KE_bottom. mgh = 0.5mv². v = √(2gh). v = √(2 × 9.81 × 3) = 7.67 m/s.

79. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: In an elastic collision, momentum and kinetic energy are conserved. Using momentum conservation, (3 × 4) = (3 × 2) + (2 × v). v = 5 m/s.

80. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Using τ = Iα, α = τ/I = 2/0.5 = 4 rad/s². Final angular velocity ω = ω₀ + αt = 10 + (4 × 5) = 20 rad/s.

81. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: Natural frequency f = (1/2π)√(k/m). f = (1/2π)√(200/0.5) ≈ 12.7 Hz.

82. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Use θ = ω₀t + 0.5αt². 10 = (2)t + 0.5(3)t². Solving, t = 3 seconds.

83. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Work done against gravity is given by W = mgh. W = (50)(9.81)(10) = 4900 J.

84. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Using impulse-momentum theorem, F_avg = (mΔv)/Δt. F_avg = (1000 × (0 - 20))/5 = 4000 N.

85. Correct Answer: D
   Explanation: θ = ω₀t + 0.5αt². θ = 0 + 0.5(2)(10)² = 100 radians. Number of revolutions = θ/(2π) = 100/(2π) ≈ 31.8 revolutions.

86. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Maximum velocity v_max = Aω, where ω = 2πf. v_max = 0.1 × 2π × 5 ≈ 3.14 m/s.

87. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Power = Work / Time. Work = KE = 0.5mv² = 0.5(500)(30²). Power = (225,000) / 15 = 30,000 W or 30 kW.

88. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Rotational kinetic energy K = 0.5Iω². 250 = 0.5I(10²). I = 250 / 50 = 2.5 kg·m².

89. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: For a rod rotating about one end, I = (1/3)ml². I = (1/3)(5)(2²) = 20/3 kg·m². K = 0.5Iω² = 0.5(20/3)(4²) = 320 J.

90. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: Impulse = Δp = m(v₂ - v₁). Δp = 0.2(10 - (-15)) = 0.2 × 25 = 5 Ns.

91. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Momentum conservation: (1000 × 20) = (1000 × 10) + (1000 × v). v = 30 m/s.

92. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: The formula for distance under uniform acceleration is s = (1/2) * a * t². Substituting a = 3 m/s² and t = 10 s gives s = (1/2) * 3 * 10² = 150 m.

93. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: The net force is F_net = applied force - friction force. Friction force = μ_k * m * g = 0.3 * 5 * 9.8 = 14.7 N. Net force = 20 - 14.7 = 5.3 N. Acceleration = F_net / m = 5.3 / 5 = 1.4 m/s².

94. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Using conservation of energy, potential energy is converted to kinetic energy: m * g * h = (1/2) * m * v². Solving for v gives v = √(2 * g * h) = √(2 * 9.8 * 5) = 7.0 m/s.

95. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Using the principle of conservation of momentum, initial momentum = final momentum. (10,000 * 40) + (15,000 * 0) = (10,000 + 15,000) * v. Solving for v gives v = 16 m/s.

96. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Total kinetic energy for rolling objects = Translational KE + Rotational KE. Translational KE = (1/2) * m * v² = (1/2) * 6 * (2²) = 12 J. Rotational KE = (1/2) * I * ω². For a solid sphere, I = (2/5) * m * r² = (2/5) * 6 * (0.4²) = 0.96 kg·m². ω = v/r = 2/0.4 = 5 rad/s. Rotational KE = (1/2) * 0.96 * (5²) = 16.8 J. Total KE = 12 + 16.8 = 28.8 J.

97. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: The period of a spring-mass system is T = 2π * √(m/k). Substituting m = 2 kg, k = 300 N/m gives T = 2π * √(2/300) ≈ 0.5 s.

98. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: Impulse = F * Δt = m * Δv. Solving for F gives F = (m * Δv) / Δt = (0.5 * 20) / 0.1 = 200 N.

99. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Angular momentum L = I * ω. For a hollow cylinder, I = m * r² = 4 * (0.3²) = 0.36 kg·m². L = 0.36 * 6 = 3.24 kg·m²/s.

100. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Time of flight T = (2 * v * sinθ) / g. Substituting v = 25 m/s, θ = 30°, g = 9.8 m/s² gives T = (2 * 25 * sin30) / 9.8 = (50 * 0.5) / 9.8 = 3.75 s.

PRACTICE TEST - FE CIVIL 3 - MECHANICS OF MATERIALS

1. A steel rod with a cross-sectional area of 50 mm² is subjected to a tensile force of 30 kN. What is the tensile stress in the rod?
   A) 600 MPa
   B) 60 MPa
   C) 300 MPa
   D) 3 MPa

2. A material has a Young's modulus of 200 GPa and a stress of 100 MPa is applied. What is the strain in the material?
   A) 0.0005
   B) 0.002
   C) 0.005
   D) 0.0001

3. A circular bar of length 2 m and diameter 10 mm is subjected to an axial tensile force of 10 kN. If the Young’s modulus is 200 GPa, what is the elongation of the bar?
   A) 0.1 mm
   B) 0.2 mm
   C) 1 mm
   D) 2 mm

4. A rectangular beam is subjected to a shear force of 15 kN. If the cross-sectional dimensions of the beam are 100 mm × 200 mm, what is the average shear stress?
   A) 0.75 MPa
   B) 1.5 MPa
   C) 2.5 MPa
   D) 7.5 MPa

5. A solid circular shaft with a diameter of 50 mm is subjected to a torque of 200 Nm. What is the maximum shear stress in the shaft?
   A) 10.2 MPa
   B) 16.2 MPa
   C) 20.4 MPa
   D) 25.5 MPa

6. A simply supported beam with a span of 6 m carries a uniformly distributed load of 2 kN/m. What is the maximum bending moment?
   A) 6 kNm
   B) 9 kNm
   C) 12 kNm
   D) 18 kNm

7. A cantilever beam of length 4 m carries a point load of 10 kN at its free end. If the flexural rigidity (EI) is 500 kNm², what is the deflection at the free end?
   A) 32 mm
   B) 40 mm
   C) 50 mm
   D) 64 mm

8. A beam is subjected to both an axial tensile force of 50 kN and a bending moment of 10 kNm. What is the nature of the stress at the extreme fiber?
   A) Axial stress only
   B) Bending stress only
   C) Combined axial and bending stress
   D) Shear stress only

9. A steel column with a modulus of elasticity of 210 GPa and pinned at both ends has a length of 4 m and a radius of gyration of 50 mm. What is the critical buckling load?
   A) 2.07 kN
   B) 20.7 kN
   C) 207 kN
   D) 2,070 kN

10. A plane stress condition has normal stresses σ_x = 100 MPa, σ_y = 50 MPa, and shear stress τ_xy = 40 MPa. What is the maximum shear stress?
   A) 45 MPa
   B) 50 MPa
   C) 65 MPa
   D) 80 MPa

11. A cylindrical rod with a length of 1.5 m and diameter of 40 mm is subjected to a compressive force of 25 kN. What is the compressive stress in the rod?
   A) 12.5 MPa
   B) 19.9 MPa
   C) 5.0 MPa
   D) 25.0 MPa

12. A rectangular cross-section beam is subjected to a shear force of 12 kN. If the beam's cross-sectional width is 80 mm and depth is 200 mm, what is the maximum shear stress?
   A) 3.75 MPa
   B) 2.5 MPa
   C) 4.2 MPa
   D) 5.0 MPa

13. A hollow circular shaft with an outer diameter of 60 mm and inner diameter of 40 mm is subjected to a torque of 150 Nm. What is the maximum shear stress in the shaft?
   A) 12.7 MPa
   B) 9.3 MPa
   C) 19.1 MPa
   D) 15.0 MPa

14. A cantilever beam of length 3 m is subjected to a uniformly distributed load of 5 kN/m. What is the maximum deflection at the free end if the flexural rigidity (EI) is 200 kN·m²?
   A) 25 mm
   B) 35 mm
   C) 40 mm
   D) 50 mm

15. Under a plane stress condition, σ_x = 60 MPa, σ_y = 30 MPa, and τ_xy = 20 MPa. What is the maximum principal stress?
   A) 75 MPa
   B) 90 MPa
   C) 50 MPa
   D) 80 MPa

   A) 27.6 kN
   B) 30.0 kN
   C) 24.8 kN
   D) 22.4 kN

   A) 1.5 MPa
   B) 2.0 MPa
   C) 3.0 MPa
   D) 2.5 MPa

18. A bar of length 1.2 m and cross-sectional area of 400 mm² is subjected to an axial load of 50 kN. If the Young's modulus is 210 GPa, what is the strain energy stored in the bar?
   A) 0.071 J
   B) 0.084 J
   C) 0.091 J
   D) 0.067 J

   A) 120 MPa
   B) 100 MPa
   C) 85 MPa
   D) 150 MPa

99. A steel plate with a length of 2.5 m is subjected to a temperature decrease of 30°C. The coefficient of thermal expansion for steel is 12 × 10⁻⁶/°C, and Young's modulus is 200 GPa. What is the thermal stress developed in the plate if it is restrained from contracting?
   A) 72 MPa
   B) 60 MPa
   C) 90 MPa
   D) 150 MPa

100. A steel column with fixed-free ends has a length of 4 m and a radius of gyration of 30 mm. If the modulus of elasticity is 210 GPa, what is the critical buckling load?
   A) 98.5 kN
   B) 197 kN
   C) 49.25 kN
   D) 123 kN



--- CORRECT ANSWERS AND EXPLANATIONS ---

1. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Tensile stress (σ) is calculated as force (F) divided by cross-sectional area (A). σ = F/A = (30 × 10³ N) / (50 × 10⁻⁶ m²) = 60 MPa.

2. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Strain (ε) is calculated as stress (σ) divided by Young's modulus (E). ε = σ/E = (100 × 10⁶ Pa) / (200 × 10⁹ Pa) = 0.0005.

3. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: Elongation (ΔL) is given by ΔL = (F × L) / (A × E). A = πd²/4 = π(0.01 m)²/4. ΔL = (10 × 10³ N × 2 m) / [(π(0.01)²/4) × 200 × 10⁹ Pa] = 0.001 m = 1 mm.

4. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Shear stress (τ) is calculated as τ = V/A. A = 100 × 200 = 20,000 mm² = 0.02 m². τ = (15 × 10³) / 0.02 = 0.75 MPa.

5. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Maximum shear stress (τ_max) in a circular shaft is given by τ_max = (T × r) / J, where J = πd⁴/32. J = π(0.05)⁴/32, r = 0.025 m. τ_max = (200 × 0.025) / (π(0.05)⁴/32) = 16.2 MPa.

6. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: The maximum bending moment for a beam with a UDL is M_max = (wL²)/8. M_max = (2 × 6²)/8 = 12 kNm.

7. Correct Answer: D
   Explanation: Deflection (δ) at the free end of a cantilever under a point load is δ = (PL³) / (3EI). δ = (10 × 4³) / (3 × 500) = 64 mm.

8. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: The stress at the extreme fiber is a combination of axial stress (σ = F/A) and bending stress (σ = Mc/I). Thus, the nature of stress is combined.

9. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: Critical buckling load is given by P_cr = (π²EI) / (KL)². I = Ar². Substituting known values results in P_cr = 207 kN.

10. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Maximum shear stress is τ_max = √[((σ_x - σ_y)/2)² + τ_xy²]. Substituting values yields τ_max = 50 MPa.

11. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Compressive stress is calculated using σ = F / A, where A is the cross-sectional area of the rod. A = πd²/4 = π(0.04)²/4 = 0.001257 m². Stress = 25,000 N / 0.001257 m² = 19.9 MPa.

12. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Maximum shear stress in a rectangular section is τ_max = 1.5 * (V / A), where A = width * depth = 0.08 m * 0.2 m = 0.016 m². τ_max = 1.5 * (12,000 N / 0.016 m²) = 3.75 MPa.

13. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: For a hollow shaft, τ_max = (T * r_outer) / J. Polar moment of inertia J = π/32 * (d_outer^4 - d_inner^4). r_outer = 0.03 m, J = π/32 * ((0.06)^4 - (0.04)^4) = 1.256 x 10^-6 m^4. τ_max = (150 N·m * 0.03 m) / 1.256 x 10^-6 m^4 = 12.7 MPa.

14. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Maximum deflection for a cantilever beam with UDL is δ_max = (wL^4) / (8EI). δ_max = (5,000 N/m * (3 m)^4) / (8 * 200,000 N·m²) = 0.025 m = 25 mm.

15. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Principal stresses are calculated using σ_1,2 = (σ_x + σ_y)/2 ± √[((σ_x - σ_y)/2)² + τ_xy²]. σ_1 = (60 + 30)/2 + √[((60 - 30)/2)² + (20)²] = 75 MPa.

16. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Critical buckling load is given by P_cr = π²EI / (L²). P_cr = π² * (210 x 10^9 N/m²) * (1.2 x 10^-6 m⁴) / (3 m)^2 = 27,600 N = 27.6 kN.

17. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: Max compressive stress = σ_axial + σ_bending. σ_axial = F / A = 10,000 N / (0.1 m * 0.2 m) = 0.5 MPa. σ_bending = M*y/I, I = bd³/12 = 0.1 * (0.2)³/12 = 6.67 x 10^-5 m⁴. y = d/2 = 0.1 m. σ_bending = (5,000 N·m * 0.1 m) / 6.67 x 10^-5 m⁴ = 2.5 MPa. Total = 0.5 + 2.5 = 3.0 MPa.

18. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Strain energy U = (F²L) / (2AE). F = 50,000 N, L = 1.2 m, A = 0.0004 m², E = 210 x 10^9 N/m². U = (50,000² * 1.2) / (2 * 0.0004 * 210 x 10^9) = 0.071 J.

19. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Thermal stress σ = E * α * ΔT. σ = (200 x 10^9 N/m²) * (12 x 10^-6 /°C) * 50°C = 120 MPa.

20. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: Radius of Mohr's circle, R = √[((σ_x - σ_y)/2)² + τ_xy²]. R = √[((80 - 40)/2)² + (30)²] = 50 MPa.

21. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Normal stress is calculated as force divided by cross-sectional area. Force = 40 kN, Area = 200 mm x 100 mm = 20000 mm². Stress = 40,000 N / 20000 mm² = 20 MPa.

22. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Strain is calculated as the change in length divided by the original length. Strain = 1 mm / 2000 mm = 0.001.

23. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: Maximum deflection for a simply supported beam with a concentrated load at the midpoint is calculated using the formula δmax = (P × L³) / (48 × EI). Substitute P = 10 kN, L = 8 m, and EI = 20 kNm² to find δmax = 40 mm.

24. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Maximum shear stress in a hollow circular shaft is calculated using τmax = T × r_outer / J, where J is the polar moment of inertia. Calculate J = π/32 × (d_outer⁴ - d_inner⁴), then substitute the values to find τmax.

25. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Critical buckling load is calculated as Pcr = π² × E × I / (L²), where I is the moment of inertia. Using I = A × r²/4 and substituting values gives Pcr = 15 kN.

26. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Hoop stress is calculated as σ_hoop = (P × r) / t, where P = 2 MPa, r = 0.6 m (outer radius), and t = 10 mm. Substituting values gives σ_hoop = 240 MPa.

27. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Thermal stress is calculated as σ_thermal = α × ΔT × E. Substituting α = 12 x 10⁻⁶ /°C, ΔT = 40°C, and E = 200 GPa gives σ_thermal = 96 MPa.

28. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Average shear stress is calculated as τ_avg = V / A, where V = 30 kN and A = width × height = 100 mm × 200 mm. Substituting values gives τ_avg = 1.5 MPa.

29. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: The radius of Mohr’s circle is calculated as R = √(((σ_x - σ_y)/2)² + τ_xy²). Substituting values gives R = 25 MPa.

30. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Compressive stress is calculated as σ = P / A, where P = 1000 kN and A = 0.5 m². Substituting values gives σ = 2 MPa.

31. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: The normal stress is calculated as force divided by the cross-sectional area. Area = 250 mm x 10 mm = 2500 mm², Stress = 60,000 N / 2500 mm² = 24 MPa.

32. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: The average shear stress is calculated as shear force divided by the cross-sectional area. Area = 120 mm x 300 mm = 36,000 mm², Shear Stress = 25,000 N / 36,000 mm² = 0.833 MPa.

33. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Maximum shear stress, τ = T*r / J, where J = πd⁴/32. Diameter = 80 mm, radius = 40 mm, J = π(80 mm)⁴/32 = 1.29x10⁶ mm⁴. τ = (300 Nm * 40 mm) / 1.29x10⁶ mm⁴ = 5.97 MPa.

34. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: For a simply supported beam with a point load at the center, maximum deflection δ = (P*L³) / (48*EI). δ = (20*5³) / (48*200) = 0.025 m.

35. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: The critical load for buckling is given by P_cr = π²EI / (KL)². For a fixed-free column, K = 2. P_cr = π²(200x10³)(1x10⁷) / (2*3x10³)² = 32.9 kN.

36. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: Thermal stress = E * α * ΔT. Stress = (210x10³)(11x10⁻⁶)(60) = 180 MPa.

37. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: The maximum stress occurs at the extreme fiber. σ = (P/A) + (M*y/I). A = 100x200 = 20000 mm², I = (100x200³)/12 = 6.67x10⁵ mm⁴, y = 200/2 = 100 mm. σ = (15000/20000) + (6000*100/6.67x10⁵) = 6.75 MPa.

38. Correct Answer: D
   Explanation: Principal stresses are calculated using σ₁,₂ = [(σ_x + σ_y)/2] ± √[((σ_x - σ_y)/2)² + τ_xy²]. σ₁ = [(100+60)/2] + √[((100-60)/2)² + 30²] = 150 MPa.

39. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Hoop stress = (P*r)/t. r = 1.0/2 = 0.5 m, t = 15 mm = 0.015 m. Stress = (2x0.5)/0.015 = 66.67 MPa.

40. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Modulus of resilience = σ²_y / (2E). Resilience = 360²/(2*180x10³) = 0.72 MJ/m³.

41. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Tensile stress is calculated as Force/Area. The cross-sectional area of the rod is π*(d/2)^2 = π*(25/2)^2 mm² = 490.87 mm². Tensile stress = 12,000 N / 490.87 mm² = 24 MPa.

42. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Maximum deflection for a uniformly loaded simply supported beam is given by δ_max = (5wL^4)/(384EI). Substituting w=1 kN/m, L=5 m, EI=500 kNm², δ_max = (5*1*5^4)/(384*500) = 7.8 mm.

43. Correct Answer: A

44. Correct Answer: B

54. Correct Answer: C

55. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: The critical buckling load is calculated using P_cr = (π²*E*I)/(L_eff²). For fixed-fixed ends, L_eff = L/2. Substituting the values yields P_cr = 105 kN.

56. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: Maximum compressive stress is calculated using σ_max = P/A + M*c/I. Substituting the values yields σ_max = 8.7 MPa.

57. Correct Answer: A

61. Correct Answer: A

62. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: For a uniformly distributed load on a simply supported beam, maximum bending moment = (w × L²) / 8. Here, w = 2 kN/m and L = 6 m. M = (2 × 6²) / 8 = 18 kNm.

63. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Shear stress in a hollow shaft is calculated as τ_max = (T × r) / J. Polar moment of inertia, J = π / 32 × (d_outer⁴ - d_inner⁴). Substitute values to find τ_max.

64. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Shear modulus (G) is calculated as G = E / [2 × (1 + ν)]. Substituting E = 210 GPa and ν = 0.3, G = 210 / [2 × (1 + 0.3)] = 81.25 GPa.

65. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Thermal expansion is calculated as ΔL = α × L × ΔT. Substituting ΔL = 1.5 mm, L = 2500 mm, ΔT = 50°C, α = ΔL / (L × ΔT) = 1.5 / (2500 × 50) = 15 × 10⁻⁶ /°C.

66. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Critical buckling load is calculated using Euler's formula: P_cr = π² × E × I / (K × L)². Substitute values with K = 2 for fixed-free ends.

67. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Angle of twist θ = (T × L) / (J × G). Polar moment of inertia J = π × d⁴ / 32. Substitute values to calculate θ.

68. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Stress amplitude is calculated as (σ_max - σ_min) / 2. Substituting σ_max = 400 MPa and σ_min = 100 MPa, stress amplitude = (400 - 100) / 2 = 200 MPa.

69. Correct Answer: D
   Explanation: Deflection at the free end of a cantilever beam under a point load is δ = (P × L³) / (3 × E × I). Substitute values for P, L, and EI to calculate δ.

70. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Combined stress is calculated by summing axial stress and bending stress. Axial stress = P / A, and bending stress = M × c / I. Substitute values to find maximum stress.

71. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Axial stress is calculated using the formula σ = F/A. With F = 50 kN and A = 300 mm², σ = (50 × 10³) / (300 × 10⁻⁶) = 166.67 MPa.

72. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: The maximum deflection for a simply supported beam under a uniformly distributed load is δ_max = (5wL⁴) / (384EI). Substituting w = 2, L = 6, and EI = 1 × 10⁴, δ_max = 16 mm.

73. Correct Answer: D
   Explanation: Maximum shear stress in a solid shaft is τ_max = (T*r) / J. With T = 500 Nm, r = 30 mm, and J = πd⁴/32 = π(0.06)⁴/32, τ_max = 62.8 MPa.

74. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Thermal elongation is calculated as ΔL = αLΔT. Substituting α = 12 × 10⁻⁶, L = 2 m, and ΔT = 50°C, ΔL = 1.2 mm.

75. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Critical buckling load is P_cr = π²(EI) / (L²). Substituting E = 200 × 10⁹, I = 5 × 10⁻⁶, and L = 4 m, P_cr = 196 kN.

76. Correct Answer: D
   Explanation: Maximum shear stress is τ_max = √[((σ_x - σ_y)/2)² + τ_xy²]. Substituting the values, τ_max = 60 MPa.

77. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Maximum normal stress is σ_max = σ_bending + σ_axial. Substituting σ_bending = M/S = (4 × 10³)/(2 × 10⁶) and σ_axial = F/A = (10 × 10³)/(300 × 10⁻⁶), σ_max = 66.7 MPa.

78. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Maximum bending moment for a cantilever beam under uniformly distributed load is M_max = wL²/2. Substituting w = 3 and L = 2, M_max = 9 kNm.

79. Correct Answer: A

80. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Allowable stress is calculated as σ_allow = yield_strength / safety_factor. Substituting yield_strength = 300 MPa and safety_factor = 2, σ_allow = 150 MPa.

81. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: The maximum bending moment for a triangular load occurs at the location of maximum intensity. Using the formula for triangular distributed loads, the maximum bending moment is calculated as WL/6. Substituting the values, M = (3 kN/m × 4 m) × (4 m / 6) = 12 kNm.

82. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Stress is calculated using the formula σ = F/A, where A = πd²/4. Substituting, A = π × (0.02 m)² / 4 = 3.14 × 0.0004 / 4 = 0.000314 m². Stress = 50,000 N / 0.000314 m² = 125 MPa.

83. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: The maximum shear stress in a hollow circular shaft is given by τ = (T * r_outer) / (π * (r_outer⁴ - r_inner⁴)). After calculating using the given dimensions and torque, τ = 40.8 MPa.

84. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Maximum bending stress is calculated using the formula σ = M*c/I, where c = h/2 and I = (b*h³)/12. Substituting the values, σ = (5000 Nm × 0.1 m) / ((1/12) × 0.1 m × (0.2 m)³) = 125 MPa.

85. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Hoop stress is calculated using σ_h = (p * r) / t. Substituting the values, σ_h = (2 MPa * 0.6 m) / 0.02 m = 120 MPa.

86. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Maximum deflection for a cantilever beam under uniform load is δ = (w * L⁴) / (8 * E * I). Converting values to consistent units and substituting, δ = 10.42 mm.

87. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Stress is calculated using σ = F/A. Substituting, σ = 500,000 N / 0.25 m² = 2 MPa.

88. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Average shear stress is calculated using τ = V/A. Substituting, A = 0.15 m × 0.3 m = 0.045 m² and τ = 40,000 N / 0.045 m² = 1.78 MPa.

89. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Using the formula E = σ/ε = (F/A) / (δ/L). After substituting values and calculating, E = 200 GPa.

90. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: Using static equilibrium equations, sum of moments about the right support determines the reaction force at the left support. Calculations yield 6.67 kN.

91. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Normal stress is calculated using the formula σ = P/A. Here, the area A = 100 mm × 50 mm = 5000 mm² = 5 × 10⁻⁴ m². Force P = 80 kN = 80 × 10³ N. σ = (80 × 10³) / (5 × 10⁻⁴) = 16 × 10⁶ Pa = 16 MPa.

92. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: The maximum bending moment for a simply supported beam with a point load at the center is given by M = (P × L) / 4. Here, P = 10 kN and L = 4 m. M = (10 × 4) / 4 = 40 / 4 = 20 kNm.

93. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: Average shear stress is calculated using τ = V / A. Shear force V = 30 kN = 30 × 10³ N. Area for shear is the perimeter of the hollow section multiplied by wall thickness: A = 2[(150 + 300) - 2 × 20] × 20 = 13600 mm² = 1.36 × 10⁻² m². τ = (30 × 10³) / (1.36 × 10⁻²) = 3 × 10⁶ Pa = 3 MPa.

94. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Maximum shear stress in a circular shaft is calculated using τ_max = (T × r) / J. Here, r = d/2 = 40/2 = 20 mm = 0.02 m. J = πd⁴ / 32 = π(0.04)⁴ / 32 = 2.51 × 10⁻⁷ m⁴. τ_max = (200 × 0.02) / (2.51 × 10⁻⁷) = 127.3 MPa.

95. Correct Answer: D
   Explanation: Maximum normal stress due to combined loading is σ_max = σ_axial + σ_bending. Axial stress, σ_axial = P/A = (50 × 10³) / (400 × 10⁻⁶) = 125 MPa. Bending stress, σ_bending = M/S = (10 × 10³) / (200 × 10⁻⁶) = 50 MPa. Total σ_max = 125 + 50 = 175 MPa.

96. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Circumferential stress is calculated using σ_c = (P × r) / t. Here, r = d/2 = 1.2/2 = 0.6 m. t = 15 mm = 0.015 m. σ_c = (2 × 0.6) / 0.015 = 80 MPa.

97. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: Elastic strain is calculated using ε = σ / E. Here, σ = 150 MPa = 150 × 10⁶ Pa, E = 200 GPa = 200 × 10⁹ Pa. ε = (150 × 10⁶) / (200 × 10⁹) = 0.00075.

98. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Maximum deflection for a cantilever beam with UDL is δ = (w × L⁴) / (8 × EI). Here, w = 2 × 10³ N/m, L = 3 m, EI = 100 × 10³ Nm². δ = (2 × 10³ × 3⁴) / (8 × 100 × 10³) = 1.8 mm.

99. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Thermal stress is calculated using σ = α × E × ΔT. Here, α = 12 × 10⁻⁶/°C, E = 200 × 10⁹ Pa, ΔT = -30°C. σ = (12 × 10⁻⁶) × (200 × 10⁹) × (-30) = 72 MPa.

100. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: Critical buckling load is given by P_cr = (π² × E × I) / (K × L)². Here, I = r² × A; assume cross-section and intermediary values. Solve based on assumptions.

PRACTICE TEST - FE CIVIL 3 - MATERIALS

1. What is the primary purpose of using reinforcement in concrete?
   A) To increase the compressive strength of concrete
   B) To resist tensile forces in concrete
   C) To reduce the weight of the structure
   D) To prevent concrete from cracking under compression

   A) Temperature during manufacturing
   B) Carbon content
   C) Length of the steel member
   D) Coating applied to the surface

   A) Low compressive strength
   B) Tendency to absorb moisture
   C) High tensile strength
   D) Lightweight nature

   C) To bind the aggregate particles together
   D) To reduce the cost of the mixture

   B) Slump Test
   C) Tensile Test
   D) Shear Test
